# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Investigation: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

**Repository:** django/django
**Task Type:** Migration Audit (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

Django is changing the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from their current format of `[(name, email), ...]` tuples to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. This is tracked in ticket #36138. Before executing this migration, the team needs a comprehensive audit of all code that reads, validates, or processes these settings.

## Your Task

Produce a migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Every file that reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`
2. Every file that validates or type-checks the settings format
3. Every file that unpacks the tuple format (e.g., `for name, email in settings.ADMINS`)
4. All documentation references that show the old tuple format
5. Test files that use the old format in fixtures or assertions
6. Third-party compatibility concerns (what breaks for users with old-format settings)
7. A migration checklist: each file that needs changes, what change is needed

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Core code paths that consume the tuple format>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of modules/packages impacted>

## Recommendation
<Migration checklist with specific files and changes needed>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `django/core/mail/`, test files, and documentation


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

56-assistanttext-
I've completed the comprehensive migration audit report and written it to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**The Django ADMINS/MANAGERS migration is already in progress.** Django 6.0 has already implemented the transition from tuple-based `(name, email)` format to string-based email lists.

### Current Status (Django 6.0+)

✅ **All implementation work is complete:**
- Core mail functions (`mail_admins()`, `mail_managers()`) updated with backward compatibility
- Deprecation warnings (`RemovedInDjango70Warning`) issued when old tuple format is detected
- Complete test coverage for both old and new formats
- Documentation updated with new format examples and migration guide

### Files Affected

**Core Code:**
- `django/core/mail/__init__.py` - Main mail functions with format validation
- `django/utils/log.py` - AdminEmailHandler for error notifications
- `django/middleware/common.py` - BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware for broken links
- `django/core/management/commands/sendtestemail.py` - Test email command

**Documentation:**
- `docs/ref/settings.txt` - Settings reference with examples
- `docs/releases/6.0.txt` - Deprecation notice
- `docs/internals/deprecation.txt` - Removal timeline for 7.0

**Tests:**
- `tests/mail/tests.py` - 3 test suites covering migration
- `tests/mail/test_sendtestemail.py` - Management command tests
- `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` - Logging handler tests

### Pending Work (Django 7.0)

When Django 7.0 is released:
- Remove backward compatibility code (lines 166-173 in `_send_server_message()`)
- Simplify validation to only accept string format
- Remove deprecated tuple format tests
- Add removal notice to release notes

The report includes detailed code references with line numbers, migration checklist

This is a security measure to prevent :ref:`HTTP Host header attacks\n72: <host-headers-virtual-hosting>`, which are possible even under many\n73: seemingly-safe web server configurations.\n74: \n75: Values in this list can be fully qualified names (e.g. ``'www.example.com'``),\n76: in which case they will be matched against the request's ``Host`` header\n77: exactly (case-insensitive, not including port). A value beginning with a period\n78: can be used as a subdomain wildcard: ``'.example.com'`` will match\n79: ``example.com``, ``www.example.com``, and any other subdomain of\n80: ``example.com``. A value of ``'*'`` will match anything; in this case you are\n81: responsible to provide your own validation of the ``Host`` header (perhaps in a\n82: middleware; if so this middleware must be listed first in\n83: :setting:`MIDDLEWARE`).\n84: \n85: Django also allows the `fully qualified domain name (FQDN)`_ of any entries.\n86: Some browsers include a trailing dot in the ``Host`` header which Django\n87: strips when performing host validation.\n88: \n89: .. _`fully qualified domain name (FQDN)`: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fully_qualified_domain_name\n90: \n91: If the ``Host`` header (or ``X-Forwarded-Host`` if\n92: :setting:`USE_X_FORWARDED_HOST` is enabled) does not match any value in this\n93: list, the :meth:`django.http.HttpRequest.get_host` method will raise\n94: :exc:`~django.core.exceptions.SuspiciousOperation`.\n95: \n96: When :setting:`DEBUG` is ``True`` and ``ALLOWED_HOSTS`` is empty, the host\n97: is validated against ``['.localhost', '127.0.0.1', '[::1]']``.\n98: \n99: ``ALLOWED_HOSTS`` is also :ref:`checked when running tests\n100: <topics-testing-advanced-multiple-hosts>`.\n101: ",

  "content": "# Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit Report\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango is in the process of migrating the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from a tuple-based format `(name, email)` to a simple string-based email list format. This migration is already implemented as of Django 6.0, with backward compatibility maintained through Django 6.x and scheduled for full removal in Django 7.0.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe Django team determined that the name portion of the `(name, email)` tuple format was never used by Django's mail functions. The tuple format unnecessarily complicated the settings interface. The new format simply uses email address strings, allowing names to be included via standard email formatting conventions (e.g., `'\\\"Name\\\" <email@example.com>'`).\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code Paths That Consume the Format\n\n#### 1. **Core Mail Functions** (`django/core/mail/__init__.py`)\n\n**Primary Implementation: `_send_server_message()` (lines 152-191)**\n```python\ndef _send_server_message(\n    *,\n    setting_name,\n    subject,\n    message,\n    html_message=None,\n    fail_silently=False,\n    connection=None,\n):\n    recipients = getattr(settings, setting_name)\n    if not recipients:\n        return\n\n    # RemovedInDjango70Warning.\n    if all(isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2 for a in recipients):\n        warnings.warn(\n            f\"Using (name, address) pairs in the {setting_name} setting is deprecated.\"\n            \" Replace with a list of email address strings.\",\n            RemovedInDjango70Warning,\n            stacklevel=2,\n        )\n        recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]\n\n    if not isinstance(recipients, (list, tuple)) or not all(\n        isinstance(address, (str, Promise)) for address in recipients\n    ):\n        raise ImproperlyConfigured(\n            f\"The {setting_name} setting must be a list of email address strings.\"\n        )\n```\n\n**Current Status:** \u2705 Already migrated. Lines 166-173 handle backward compatibility by:\n- Detecting old tuple format via type checking\n- Issuing `RemovedInDjango70Warning` deprecation warning\n- Extracting email addresses from tuples via `[a[1] for a in recipients]`\n- Validating that final format is list of strings\n\n**Public API Functions:**\n- `mail_admins()` (lines 197-208): Calls `_send_server_message()` with setting_name=\"ADMINS\"\n- `mail_managers()` (lines 214-225): Calls `_send_server_message()` with setting_name=\"MANAGERS\"\n\n#### 2. **Error Logging Handler** (`django/utils/log.py`)\n\n**Location:** `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` (lines 94-101)\n```python\ndef emit(self, record):\n    # Early return when no email will be sent.\n    if (\n        not settings.ADMINS\n        # Method not overridden.\n        and self.send_mail.__func__ is AdminEmailHandler.send_mail\n    ):\n        return\n```\n\n**Current Status:** \u2705 Only checks if ADMINS is empty. Delegates to `mail.mail_admins()` (line 138), which handles format validation.\n\n**Impact:** Used in default Django logging configuration to send 500-error notifications to admins.\n\n#### 3. **Middleware** (`django/middleware/common.py`)\n\n**Location:** `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware.process_response()` (line 131)\n```python\nmail_managers(\n    \"Broken %slink on %s\" % (...),\n    \"Referrer: ...\",\n    fail_silently=True,\n)\n```\n\n**Current Status:** \u2705 Uses public `mail_managers()` API, which handles format validation.\n\n**Impact:** Sends broken link notifications to site managers.\n\n#### 4. **Management Command** (`django/core/management/commands/sendtestemail.py`)\n\n**Location:** Lines 42-46\n```python\nif kwargs[\"managers\"]:\n    mail_managers(subject, \"This email was sent to the site managers.\")\n\nif kwargs[\"admins\"]:\n    mail_admins(subject, \"This email was sent to the site admins.\")\n```\n\n**Current Status:** \u2705 Uses public API functions that handle format validation.\n\n**Impact:** CLI tool for testing email configuration.\n\n---\n\n### Settings Definitions\n\n**Location:** `django/conf/global_settings.py`\n\n**ADMINS Setting (lines 24-26):**\n```python\n# People who get code error notifications. They get broken link\n# notifications and other various emails.\nMANAGERS = ADMINS\n```\n\n**Current Status:** \u2705 Comments already show new string format. Default values are empty lists.\n\n---\n\n### Documentation References\n\n**1. Settings Documentation** (`docs/ref/settings.txt`)\n\n**ADMINS Setting (lines 42-61):**\n```\n``ADMINS``\n----------\n\nDefault: ``[]`` (Empty list)\n\nA list of all the people who get code error notifications. When\nDEBUG=False and AdminEmailHandler is configured in LOGGING (done by default),\nDjango emails these people the details of exceptions raised in the request/response cycle.\n\nEach item in the list should be an email address string. Example::\n\n    ADMINS = [\"john@example.com\", '\"Ng, Mary\" <mary@example.com>']\n\n.. versionchanged:: 6.0\n\n    In older versions, required a list of (name, address) tuples.\n```\n\n**MANAGERS Setting (lines 2074-2087):**\n```\n``MANAGERS``\n------------\n\nDefault: ``[]`` (Empty list)\n\nA list in the same format as ADMINS that specifies who should get\nbroken link notifications when BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware is enabled.\n\n.. versionchanged:: 6.0\n\n    In older versions, required a list of (name, address) tuples.\n```\n\n**2. Deprecation Documentation** (`docs/releases/6.0.txt`, lines 540-543)\n\n```\n* Setting :setting:`ADMINS` or :setting:`MANAGERS` to a list of (name, address)\n  tuples is deprecated. Set to a list of email address strings instead. Django\n  never used the name portion. To include a name, format the address string as\n  ``'\\\"Name\\\" <address>'`` or use Python's :func:`email.utils.formataddr`.\n```\n\n**3. # Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit Report

## Summary

Django is in the process of migrating the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from a tuple-based format `(name, email)` to a simple string-based email list format. This migration is already implemented as of Django 6.0, with backward compatibility maintained through Django 6.x and scheduled for full removal in Django 7.0.

## Root Cause

The Django team determined that the name portion of the `(name, email)` tuple format was never used by Django's mail functions. The tuple format unnecessarily complicated the settings interface. The new format simply uses email address strings, allowing names to be included via standard email formatting conventions (e.g., `'\"Name\" <email@example.com>'`).

## Evidence

### Code Paths That Consume the Format

#### 1. **Core Mail Functions** (`django/core/mail/__init__.py`)

**Primary Implementation: `_send_server_message()` (lines 152-191)**
```python
def _send_server_message(
    *,
    setting_name,
    subject,
    message,
    html_message=None,
    fail_silently=False,
    connection=None,
):
    recipients = getattr(settings, setting_name)
    if not recipients:
        return

    # RemovedInDjango70Warning.
    if all(isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2 for a in recipients):
        warnings.warn(
            f"Using (name, address) pairs in the {setting_name} setting is deprecated."
            " Replace with a list of email address strings.",
            RemovedInDjango70Warning,
            stacklevel=2,
        )
        recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]

    if not isinstance(recipients, (list, tuple)) or not all(
        isinstance(address, (str, Promise)) for address in recipients
    ):
        raise ImproperlyConfigured(
